I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Blob merge with Myers algorithm produces false conflict where git merge-file resolves cleanly
## Summary

`gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::merge` with the **Myers** diff algorithm produces a false conflict on certain inputs where `git merge-file` (also Myers-based) resolves cleanly. Switching to **Histogram** resolves the issue.

## Reproduction

Given three versions of a file:
- **base** (71 lines) - original version
- **ours** (164 lines) - heavily expanded version with ~90 new lines inserted before a comment
- **theirs** (70 lines) - identical to base except one comment line deleted

The only change in base→theirs is the deletion of a single comment line:
```diff
--- base
+++ theirs
@@ -29,7 +29,6 @@
 	const uiState = inject(UI_STATE);
 	const claudeCodeService = inject(CLAUDE_CODE_SERVICE);

-	// ── MCP config modal ─────────────────────────────────────────────
 	let mcpConfigModal = $state<CodegenMcpConfigModal>();
```

In base→ours, this same comment exists but is now at line 102 (instead of 32) because ~70 lines of new code were inserted above it. The content around it (`let mcpConfigModal`, `const mcpClaudeConfigQuery`) is unchanged.

### Expected behavior (matches `git merge-file`)

Clean merge: keep all the new code from ours, apply the comment deletion from theirs. `git merge-file` exits 0 with no conflict markers.

```sh
git merge-file -p ours.svelte base.svelte theirs.svelte
# exit 0, 163 lines, 0 conflict markers
```

### Actual behavior

`gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::merge` with `Algorithm::Myers` reports `Resolution::Conflict`:

```
<<<<<<< ours
	// ── Actions ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────
	async function onAbort() { ... }
	async function sendMessage(prompt) { ... }
	async function handleAnswerQuestion(answers) { ... }

	// ── MCP config modal ─────────────────────────────────────────────
=======
>>>>>>> theirs
```

gix sees the comment deletion as conflicting with the large insertion above it. The conflict region spans lines 78-105 of the merged output.

### Key finding: Histogram algorithm works correctly

```rust
// Myers:     Resolution::Conflict (1 false conflict marker)
// Histogram: Resolution::Complete (0 conflicts) ✓
```

This suggests the Myers implementation in imara-diff produces different hunk boundaries than git's xdiff for this input, causing the 3-way merge to see overlapping regions where git doesn't.

## Minimal reproduction code

```rust
use gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text;

let base = std::fs::read("base.svelte").unwrap();
let ours = std::fs::read("ours.svelte").unwrap();
let theirs = std::fs::read("theirs.svelte").unwrap();

let mut output = Vec::new();
let mut input = imara_diff::intern::InternedInput::new(&[][..], &[][..]);

// Myers: produces false conflict
let options = text::Options {
    diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers,
    conflict: text::Conflict::Keep {
        style: text::ConflictStyle::Merge,
        marker_size: std::num::NonZeroU8::new(7).unwrap(),
    },
};
let labels = text::Labels {
    ancestor: Some("base".into()),
    current: Some("ours".into()),
    other: Some("theirs".into()),
};
let resolution = text::function::merge(
    &mut output, &mut input, labels, &ours, &base, &theirs, options,
);
assert!(matches!(resolution, gix_merge::blob::Resolution::Conflict));
// ^ This should be Resolution::Complete to match git behavior
```

## Impact

This causes GitButler's commit amend operation to reject valid changes with `CherryPickMergeConflict` when the 3-way merge (base=workspace tree, ours=target commit tree, theirs=workspace+change) hits this code path. The user is unable to amend their change into the correct commit even though the merge is semantically clean.

## Environment

- gix 0.80.0 (from `main` branch, commit `1a72380a`)
- imara-diff 0.1.8
- macOS (Darwin 25.3.0, aarch64)

## Files

I'll attach the three `.svelte` files (base/ours/theirs) needed to reproduce.

     2	
     3	use crate::blob::{
     4	    builtin_driver::text::{
     5	        utils::{
     6	            assure_ends_with_nl, collect_hunks, contains_lines, detect_line_ending, detect_line_ending_or_nl,
     7	            fill_ancestor, hunks_differ_in_diff3, take_intersecting, tokens, write_ancestor, write_conflict_marker,
     8	            write_hunks, zealously_contract_hunks, Hunk, Side,
     9	        },
    10	        Conflict, ConflictStyle, Labels, Options,
    11	    },
    12	    Resolution,
    13	};
    14	
    15	/// Merge `current` and `other` with `ancestor` as base according to `opts`.
    16	///
    17	/// Use `labels` to annotate conflict sections.
    18	///
    19	/// `input` is for reusing memory for lists of tokens, but note that it grows indefinitely
    20	/// while tokens for `current`, `ancestor` and `other` are added.
    21	/// Place the merged result in `out` (cleared before use) and return the resolution.
    22	///
    23	/// # Important
    24	///
    25	/// *The caller* is responsible for clearing `input`, otherwise tokens will accumulate.
    26	/// This idea is to save time if the input is known to be very similar.
    27	#[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
    28	pub fn merge<'a>(
    29	    out: &mut Vec<u8>,
    30	    input: &mut imara_diff::InternedInput<&'a [u8]>,
    31	    Labels {
    32	        ancestor: ancestor_label,
    33	        current: current_label,
    34	        other: other_label,
    35	    }: Labels<'_>,
    36	    current: &'a [u8],
    37	    ancestor: &'a [u8],
    38	    other: &'a [u8],
    39	    Options {
    40	        diff_algorithm,
    41	        conflict,
    42	    }: Options,
    43	) -> Resolution {
    44	    out.clear();
    45	    input.update_before(tokens(ancestor));
    46	    input.update_after(tokens(current));
    47	
    48	    let hunks = collect_hunks(diff_algorithm, input, Side::Current, Vec::new());
    49	
    50	    let current_tokens = std::mem::take(&mut input.after);
    51	    input.update_after(tokens(other));
    52	
    53	    let mut hunks = collect_hunks(diff_algorithm, input, Side::Other, hunks);
    54	
    55	    if hunks.is_empty() {
    56	        write_ancestor(input, 0, input.before.len(), out);
    57	        return Resolution::Complete;
    58	    }
    59	
    60	    hunks.sort_by_key(|a| a.before.start);
    61	    let mut hunks = hunks.into_iter().peekable();
    62	    let mut intersecting = Vec::new();
    63	    let mut ancestor_integrated_until = 0;
    64	    let mut resolution = Resolution::Complete;
    65	    let mut current_hunks = Vec::with_capacity(2);
    66	    while take_intersecting(&mut hunks, &mut current_hunks, &mut intersecting).is_some() {
    67	        if intersecting.is_empty() {
    68	            let hunk = current_hunks.pop().expect("always pushed during intersection check");
    69	            write_ancestor(input, ancestor_integrated_until, hunk.before.start as usize, out);
    70	            ancestor_integrated_until = hunk.before.end;
    71	            write_hunks(std::slice::from_ref(&hunk), input, &current_tokens, out);
    72	            continue;
    73	        }
    74	
    75	        let filled_hunks_side = current_hunks.first().expect("at least one hunk").side;
    76	        {
    77	            let filled_hunks_range = before_range_from_hunks(&current_hunks);
    78	            let intersecting_range = before_range_from_hunks(&intersecting);
    79	            let extended_range = filled_hunks_range.start..intersecting_range.end.max(filled_hunks_range.end);
    80	            fill_ancestor(&extended_range, &mut current_hunks);
    81	            fill_ancestor(&extended_range, &mut intersecting);
    82	        }
    83	        match conflict {
    84	            Conflict::Keep { style, marker_size } => {
    85	                let marker_size = marker_size.get();
    86	                let (hunks_front_and_back, num_hunks_front) = match style {
    87	                    ConflictStyle::Merge | ConflictStyle::ZealousDiff3 => {
    88	                        zealously_contract_hunks(&mut current_hunks, &mut intersecting, input, &current_tokens)
    89	                    }
    90	                    ConflictStyle::Diff3 => (Vec::new(), 0),
    91	                };
    92	                let (our_hunks, their_hunks) = match filled_hunks_side {
    93	                    Side::Current => (&current_hunks, &intersecting),
    94	                    Side::Other => (&intersecting, &current_hunks),
    95	                    Side::Ancestor => {
    96	                        unreachable!("initial hunks are never ancestors")
    97	                    }
    98	                };
    99	                let (front_hunks, back_hunks) = hunks_front_and_back.split_at(num_hunks_front);
   100	                let first_hunk = first_hunk(front_hunks, our_hunks, their_hunks, back_hunks);
   101	                let last_hunk = last_hunk(front_hunks, our_hunks, their_hunks, back_hunks);
   102	                write_ancestor(input, ancestor_integrated_until, first_hunk.before.start as usize, out);
   103	                write_hunks(front_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   104	                // DEVIATION: this makes tests (mostly) pass, but probably is very different from what Git does.
   105	                let hunk_storage;
   106	                let nl = detect_line_ending(
   107	                    if front_hunks.is_empty() {
   108	                        hunk_storage = Hunk {
   109	                            before: ancestor_integrated_until..first_hunk.before.start,
   110	                            after: Default::default(),
   111	                            side: Side::Ancestor,
   112	                        };
   113	                        std::slice::from_ref(&hunk_storage)
   114	                    } else {
   115	                        front_hunks
   116	                    },
   117	                    input,
   118	                    &current_tokens,
   119	                )
   120	                .or_else(|| detect_line_ending(our_hunks, input, &current_tokens))
   121	                .unwrap_or(b"\n".into());
   122	                match style {
   123	                    ConflictStyle::Merge => {
   124	                        if contains_lines(our_hunks) || contains_lines(their_hunks) {
   125	                            resolution = Resolution::Conflict;
   126	                            write_conflict_marker(out, b'<', current_label, marker_size, nl);
   127	                            write_hunks(our_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   128	                            write_conflict_marker(out, b'=', None, marker_size, nl);
   129	                            write_hunks(their_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   130	                            write_conflict_marker(out, b'>', other_label, marker_size, nl);
   131	                        }
   132	                    }
   133	                    ConflictStyle::Diff3 | ConflictStyle::ZealousDiff3 => {
   134	                        if contains_lines(our_hunks) || contains_lines(their_hunks) {
   135	                            if hunks_differ_in_diff3(style, our_hunks, their_hunks, input, &current_tokens) {
   136	                                resolution = Resolution::Conflict;
   137	                                write_conflict_marker(out, b'<', current_label, marker_size, nl);
   138	                                write_hunks(our_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   139	                                let ancestor_hunk = Hunk {
   140	                                    before: first_hunk.before.start..last_hunk.before.end,
   141	                                    after: Default::default(),
   142	                                    side: Side::Ancestor,
   143	                                };
   144	                                let ancestor_hunk = std::slice::from_ref(&ancestor_hunk);
   145	                                let ancestor_nl = detect_line_ending_or_nl(ancestor_hunk, input, &current_tokens);
   146	                                write_conflict_marker(out, b'|', ancestor_label, marker_size, ancestor_nl);
   147	                                write_hunks(ancestor_hunk, input, &current_tokens, out);
   148	                                write_conflict_marker(out, b'=', None, marker_size, nl);
   149	                                write_hunks(their_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   150	                                write_conflict_marker(out, b'>', other_label, marker_size, nl);
   151	                            } else {
   152	                                write_hunks(our_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   153	                            }
   154	                        }
   155	                    }
   156	                }
   157	
   158	                write_hunks(back_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   159	                ancestor_integrated_until = last_hunk.before.end;
   160	            }
   161	            Conflict::ResolveWithOurs | Conflict::ResolveWithTheirs => {
   162	                let (our_hunks, their_hunks) = match filled_hunks_side {
   163	                    Side::Current => (&current_hunks, &intersecting),
   164	                    Side::Other => (&intersecting, &current_hunks),
   165	                    Side::Ancestor => {
   166	                        unreachable!("initial hunks are never ancestors")
   167	                    }
   168	                };
   169	                if hunks_differ_in_diff3(ConflictStyle::Diff3, our_hunks, their_hunks, input, &current_tokens) {
   170	                    resolution = Resolution::CompleteWithAutoResolvedConflict;
   171	                }
   172	                let hunks_to_write = if conflict == Conflict::ResolveWithOurs {
   173	                    our_hunks
   174	                } else {
   175	                    their_hunks
   176	                };
   177	                if let Some(first_hunk) = hunks_to_write.first() {
   178	                    write_ancestor(input, ancestor_integrated_until, first_hunk.before.start as usize, out);
   179	                }
   180	                write_hunks(hunks_to_write, input, &current_tokens, out);
   181	                if let Some(last_hunk) = hunks_to_write.last() {
   182	                    ancestor_integrated_until = last_hunk.before.end;
   183	                }
   184	            }
   185	            Conflict::ResolveWithUnion => {
   186	                let (hunks_front_and_back, num_hunks_front) =
   187	                    zealously_contract_hunks(&mut current_hunks, &mut intersecting, input, &current_tokens);
   188	
   189	                let (our_hunks, their_hunks) = match filled_hunks_side {
   190	                    Side::Current => (&current_hunks, &intersecting),
   191	                    Side::Other => (&intersecting, &current_hunks),
   192	                    Side::Ancestor => {
   193	                        unreachable!("initial hunks are never ancestors")
   194	                    }
   195	                };
   196	                if hunks_differ_in_diff3(ConflictStyle::Diff3, our_hunks, their_hunks, input, &current_tokens) {
   197	                    resolution = Resolution::CompleteWithAutoResolvedConflict;
   198	                }
   199	                let (front_hunks, back_hunks) = hunks_front_and_back.split_at(num_hunks_front);
   200	                let first_hunk = first_hunk(front_hunks, our_hunks, their_hunks, back_hunks);
   201	                write_ancestor(input, ancestor_integrated_until, first_hunk.before.start as usize, out);
   202	                write_hunks(front_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   203	                assure_ends_with_nl(out, detect_line_ending_or_nl(front_hunks, input, &current_tokens));
   204	                write_hunks(our_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   205	                assure_ends_with_nl(out, detect_line_ending_or_nl(our_hunks, input, &current_tokens));
   206	                write_hunks(their_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   207	                if !back_hunks.is_empty() {
   208	                    assure_ends_with_nl(out, detect_line_ending_or_nl(their_hunks, input, &current_tokens));
   209	                }
   210	                write_hunks(back_hunks, input, &current_tokens, out);
   211	                let last_hunk = last_hunk(front_hunks, our_hunks, their_hunks, back_hunks);
   212	                ancestor_integrated_until = last_hunk.before.end;
   213	            }
   214	        }
   215	    }
   216	    write_ancestor(input, ancestor_integrated_until, input.before.len(), out);
   217	
   218	    resolution
   219	}
   220	
   221	fn first_hunk<'a>(front: &'a [Hunk], ours: &'a [Hunk], theirs: &'a [Hunk], back: &'a [Hunk]) -> &'a Hunk {
   222	    front
   223	        .first()
   224	        .or(ours.first())
   225	        .or(theirs.first())
   226	        .or(back.first())
   227	        .expect("at least one hunk - we aborted if there are none anywhere")
   228	}
   229	
   230	/// Note that last-hunk could be [`first_hunk()`], so the hunk must only be used accordingly.
   231	fn last_hunk<'a>(front: &'a [Hunk], ours: &'a [Hunk], theirs: &'a [Hunk], back: &'a [Hunk]) -> &'a Hunk {
   232	    back.last()
   233	        .or(theirs.last())
   234	        .or(ours.last())
   235	        .or(front.last())
   236	        .expect("at least one hunk - we aborted if there are none anywhere")
   237	}
   238	
   239	fn before_range_from_hunks(hunks: &[Hunk]) -> Range<u32> {
   240	    hunks
   241	        .first()
   242	        .zip(hunks.last())
   243	        .map(|(f, l)| f.before.start..l.before.end)
   244	        .expect("at least one entry")
   245	}
   246

     7	/// Used only when `diff3` is the conflict style as `zdiff3` automatically reduces hunks into nothing.
     8	/// Here we check if all hunks are the same.
     9	pub fn hunks_differ_in_diff3(
    10	    style: ConflictStyle,
    11	    a: &[Hunk],
    12	    b: &[Hunk],
    13	    input: &imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
    14	    current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
    15	) -> bool {
    16	    if style != ConflictStyle::Diff3 {
    17	        return true;
    18	    }
    19	
    20	    let tokens_for_hunk = |hunk: &Hunk| -> &[imara_diff::Token] {
    21	        &tokens_for_side(hunk.side, input, current_tokens)[hunk.after.start as usize..hunk.after.end as usize]
    22	    };
    23	
    24	    a.iter()
    25	        .flat_map(tokens_for_hunk)
    26	        .ne(b.iter().flat_map(tokens_for_hunk))
    27	}
    28	
    29	pub fn contains_lines(hunks: &[Hunk]) -> bool {
    30	    hunks.iter().any(|h| !h.after.is_empty())
    31	}
    32	
    33	/// ## Deviation
    34	///
    35	/// This implementation definitely isn't the same as in Git, primarily because it seemed impossible
    36	/// to understand what's going on there without investing more time than it seemed worth.
    37	pub fn detect_line_ending(
    38	    hunks: &[Hunk],
    39	    input: &mut imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
    40	    current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
    41	) -> Option<&'static BStr> {
    42	    fn is_eol_crlf(
    43	        hunks: &[Hunk],
    44	        input: &mut imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
    45	        current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
    46	    ) -> Option<bool> {
    47	        let (range, side) = hunks.iter().rev().find_map(|h| {
    48	            (!h.after.is_empty())
    49	                .then_some((&h.after, h.side))
    50	                .or((!h.before.is_empty()).then_some((&h.before, Side::Ancestor)))
    51	        })?;
    52	
    53	        let tokens = tokens_for_side(side, input, current_tokens);
    54	        {
    55	            let last_line = tokens
    56	                .get(range.end as usize - 1)
    57	                .map(|token| &input.interner[*token])?;
    58	            if last_line.last() == Some(&b'\n') {
    59	                return last_line.get(last_line.len().checked_sub(2)?).map(|c| *c == b'\r');
    60	            }
    61	        }
    62	        let second_to_last_line = tokens
    63	            .get(range.end.checked_sub(2)? as usize)
    64	            .map(|token| &input.interner[*token])?;
    65	        second_to_last_line
    66	            .get(second_to_last_line.len().checked_sub(2)?)
    67	            .map(|c| *c == b'\r')
    68	    }
    69	    is_eol_crlf(hunks, input, current_tokens).map(|is_crlf| if is_crlf { b"\r\n".into() } else { b"\n".into() })
    70	}
    71	
    72	pub fn detect_line_ending_or_nl(
    73	    hunks: &[Hunk],
    74	    input: &mut imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
    75	    current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
    76	) -> &'static BStr {
    77	    detect_line_ending(hunks, input, current_tokens).unwrap_or(b"\n".into())
    78	}
    79	
    80	fn tokens_for_side<'a>(
    81	    side: Side,
    82	    input: &'a imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
    83	    current_tokens: &'a [imara_diff::Token],
    84	) -> &'a [imara_diff::Token] {
    85	    match side {
    86	        Side::Current => current_tokens,
    87	        Side::Other => &input.after,
    88	        Side::Ancestor => &input.before,
    89	    }
    90	}
    91	
    92	pub fn assure_ends_with_nl(out: &mut Vec<u8>, nl: &BStr) {
    93	    if !out.is_empty() && !out.ends_with(b"\n") {
    94	        out.push_str(nl);
    95	    }
    96	}
    97	
    98	pub fn write_conflict_marker(out: &mut Vec<u8>, marker: u8, label: Option<&BStr>, marker_size: u8, nl: &BStr) {
    99	    assure_ends_with_nl(out, nl);
   100	    out.extend(std::iter::repeat_n(marker, marker_size as usize));
   101	    if let Some(label) = label {
   102	        out.push(b' ');
   103	        out.extend_from_slice(label);
   104	    }
   105	    out.push_str(nl);
   106	}
   107	
   108	pub fn write_ancestor(input: &imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>, from: u32, to: usize, out: &mut Vec<u8>) {
   109	    if to < from as usize {
   110	        return;
   111	    }
   112	    if let Some(tokens) = input.before.get(from as usize..to) {
   113	        write_tokens(&input.interner, tokens, out);
   114	    }
   115	}
   116	
   117	/// Look at all hunks in `in_out` and fill in the ancestor in the range of `ancestor_range`.
   118	/// This is all based on knowing the ranges are sequences of tokens.
   119	pub fn fill_ancestor(Range { start, end }: &Range<u32>, in_out: &mut Vec<Hunk>) {
   120	    fn is_nonzero(num: &u32) -> bool {
   121	        *num > 0
   122	    }
   123	    if in_out.is_empty() {
   124	        return;
   125	    }
   126	    let first = &in_out[0];
   127	    let mut first_idx = 0;
   128	    if let Some(lines_to_add) = first.before.start.checked_sub(*start).filter(is_nonzero) {
   129	        in_out.insert(0, ancestor_hunk(*start, lines_to_add));
   130	        first_idx += 1;
   131	    }
   132	
   133	    let mut added_hunks = false;
   134	    for (idx, next_idx) in (first_idx..in_out.len()).map(|idx| (idx, idx + 1)) {
   135	        let Some(next_hunk) = in_out.get(next_idx) else { break };
   136	        let hunk = &in_out[idx];
   137	        if let Some(lines_to_add) = next_hunk.before.start.checked_sub(hunk.before.end).filter(is_nonzero) {
   138	            in_out.push(ancestor_hunk(hunk.before.end, lines_to_add));
   139	            added_hunks = true;
   140	        }
   141	    }
   142	    let in_out_len = in_out.len();
   143	    if added_hunks {
   144	        in_out[first_idx..in_out_len].sort_by_key(|hunk| hunk.before.start);
   145	    }
   146	
   147	    let last = &in_out[in_out_len - 1];
   148	    if let Some(lines_to_add) = end.checked_sub(last.before.end).filter(is_nonzero) {
   149	        in_out.push(ancestor_hunk(last.before.end, lines_to_add));
   150	    }
   151	}
   152	
   153	fn ancestor_hunk(start: u32, num_lines: u32) -> Hunk {
   154	    let range = start..start + num_lines;
   155	    Hunk {
   156	        before: range.clone(),
   157	        after: range,
   158	        side: Side::Ancestor,
   159	    }
   160	}
   161	
   162	/// Reduce the area of `a_hunks` and the hunks in `b_hunks` so that only those lines that are
   163	/// actually different remain. Note that we have to compare the resolved values, not only the tokens,
   164	/// so `current_tokens` is expected to be known to the `input` (and its `interner`).
   165	/// Hunks from all input arrays maybe removed in the process from the front and back, in case they
   166	/// are entirely equal to each other.
   167	/// Note also that `a_hunks` and `b_hunks` are treated to be consecutive, so [`fill_ancestor()`] must
   168	/// have been called beforehand, and are assumed to cover the same space in the ancestor buffer.
   169	///
   170	/// Return a new vector of all the hunks that were removed from front and back, with partial hunks inserted,
   171	/// along with the amount of hunks that go front, with the remaining going towards the back.
   172	#[must_use]
   173	pub fn zealously_contract_hunks(
   174	    a_hunks: &mut Vec<Hunk>,
   175	    b_hunks: &mut Vec<Hunk>,
   176	    input: &imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
   177	    current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
   178	) -> (Vec<Hunk>, usize) {
   179	    let line_content = |token_idx: u32, side: Side| {
   180	        let tokens = match side {
   181	            Side::Current => current_tokens,
   182	            Side::Other => &input.after,
   183	            Side::Ancestor => &input.before,
   184	        };
   185	        &input.interner[tokens[token_idx as usize]]
   186	    };
   187	    let (mut last_a_hunk_idx, mut last_b_hunk_idx) = (0, 0);
   188	    let (mut out, hunks_in_front) = {
   189	        let (mut remove_leading_a_hunks_from, mut remove_leading_b_hunks_from) = (None, None);
   190	        let (mut a_hunk_token_equal_till, mut b_hunk_token_equal_till) = (None, None);
   191	        for ((a_token_idx, a_hunk_idx, a_hunk_side), (b_token_idx, b_hunk_idx, b_hunk_side)) in
   192	            iterate_hunks(a_hunks).zip(iterate_hunks(b_hunks))
   193	        {
   194	            let a_line = line_content(a_token_idx, a_hunk_side).as_bstr();
   195	            let b_line = line_content(b_token_idx, b_hunk_side).as_bstr();
   196	
   197	            if last_a_hunk_idx != a_hunk_idx {
   198	                a_hunk_token_equal_till = None;
   199	                last_a_hunk_idx = a_hunk_idx;
   200	            }
   201	            if last_b_hunk_idx != b_hunk_idx {
   202	                b_hunk_token_equal_till = None;
   203	                last_b_hunk_idx = b_hunk_idx;
   204	            }
   205	            if a_line == b_line {
   206	                (remove_leading_a_hunks_from, remove_leading_b_hunks_from) = (Some(a_hunk_idx), Some(b_hunk_idx));
   207	                (a_hunk_token_equal_till, b_hunk_token_equal_till) = (Some(a_token_idx), Some(b_token_idx));
   208	            } else {
   209	                break;
   210	            }
   211	        }
   212	
   213	        let mut out = Vec::with_capacity(remove_leading_a_hunks_from.unwrap_or_else(|| {
   214	            if a_hunk_token_equal_till.is_some() {
   215	                1
   216	            } else {
   217	                0
   218	            }
   219	        }));
   220	        truncate_hunks_from_from_front(
   221	            a_hunks,
   222	            remove_leading_a_hunks_from,
   223	            a_hunk_token_equal_till,
   224	            Some(&mut out),
   225	        );
   226	        truncate_hunks_from_from_front(b_hunks, remove_leading_b_hunks_from, b_hunk_token_equal_till, None);
   227	        let hunks_in_front = out.len();
   228	        (out, hunks_in_front)
   229	    };
   230	
   231	    (last_a_hunk_idx, last_b_hunk_idx) = (0, 0);
   232	    {
   233	        let (mut remove_trailing_a_hunks_from, mut remove_trailing_b_hunks_from) = (None, None);
   234	        let (mut a_hunk_token_equal_from, mut b_hunk_token_equal_from) = (None, None);
   235	        for ((a_token_idx, a_hunk_idx, a_hunk_side), (b_token_idx, b_hunk_idx, b_hunk_side)) in
   236	            iterate_hunks_rev(a_hunks).zip(iterate_hunks_rev(b_hunks))
   237	        {
   238	            let a_line = line_content(a_token_idx, a_hunk_side).as_bstr();
   239	            let b_line = line_content(b_token_idx, b_hunk_side).as_bstr();
   240	
   241	            if last_a_hunk_idx != a_hunk_idx {
   242	                a_hunk_token_equal_from = None;
   243	                last_a_hunk_idx = a_hunk_idx;
   244	            }
   245	            if last_b_hunk_idx != b_hunk_idx {
   246	                b_hunk_token_equal_from = None;
   247	                last_b_hunk_idx = b_hunk_idx;
   248	            }
   249	
   250	            if a_line == b_line {
   251	                (remove_trailing_a_hunks_from, remove_trailing_b_hunks_from) = (Some(a_hunk_idx), Some(b_hunk_idx));
   252	                (a_hunk_token_equal_from, b_hunk_token_equal_from) = (Some(a_token_idx), Some(b_token_idx));
   253	            } else {
   254	                break;
   255	            }
   256	        }
   257	
   258	        truncate_hunks_from_from_back(
   259	            a_hunks,
   260	            remove_trailing_a_hunks_from,
   261	            a_hunk_token_equal_from,
   262	            Some(&mut out),
   263	        );
   264	        truncate_hunks_from_from_back(b_hunks, remove_trailing_b_hunks_from, b_hunk_token_equal_from, None);
   265	    }
   266	
   267	    (out, hunks_in_front)
   268	}
   269	
   270	fn range_by_side(hunk: &mut Hunk) -> &mut Range<u32> {
   271	    match hunk.side {
   272	        Side::Current | Side::Other => &mut hunk.after,
   273	        Side::Ancestor => &mut hunk.before,
   274	    }
   275	}
   276	fn truncate_hunks_from_from_front(
   277	    hunks: &mut Vec<Hunk>,
   278	    hunks_to_remove_until_idx: Option<usize>,
   279	    hunk_token_equal_till: Option<u32>,
   280	    mut out_hunks: Option<&mut Vec<Hunk>>,
   281	) {
   282	    let Some(hunks_to_remove_until_idx) = hunks_to_remove_until_idx else {
   283	        assert!(hunk_token_equal_till.is_none());
   284	        return;
   285	    };
   286	    let mut last_index_to_remove = Some(hunks_to_remove_until_idx);
   287	    let hunk = &mut hunks[hunks_to_remove_until_idx];
   288	    let range = range_by_side(hunk);
   289	    if let Some(hunk_token_equal_till) = hunk_token_equal_till {
   290	        let orig_start = range.start;
   291	        let new_start = hunk_token_equal_till + 1;
   292	        range.start = new_start;
   293	        if Range::<u32>::is_empty(range) {
   294	            range.start = orig_start;
   295	        } else if let Some(out) = out_hunks.as_deref_mut() {
   296	            last_index_to_remove = hunks_to_remove_until_idx.checked_sub(1);
   297	            let mut removed_hunk = hunk.clone();
   298	            let new_range = range_by_side(&mut removed_hunk);
   299	
   300	            new_range.start = orig_start;
   301	            new_range.end = new_start;
   302	
   303	            out.push(removed_hunk);
   304	        } else {
   305	            last_index_to_remove = hunks_to_remove_until_idx.checked_sub(1);
   306	        }
   307	    }
   308	    if let Some(last_index_to_remove) = last_index_to_remove {
   309	        let mut current_idx = 0;
   310	        hunks.retain(|hunk| {
   311	            if current_idx > last_index_to_remove {
   312	                true
   313	            } else {
   314	                current_idx += 1;
   315	                if let Some(out) = out_hunks.as_deref_mut() {
   316	                    out.push(hunk.clone());
   317	                }
   318	                false
   319	            }
   320	        });
   321	    }
   322	}
   323	
   324	fn truncate_hunks_from_from_back(
   325	    hunks: &mut Vec<Hunk>,
   326	    remove_trailing_hunks_from_idx: Option<usize>,
   327	    hunk_token_equal_from: Option<u32>,
   328	    mut out_hunks: Option<&mut Vec<Hunk>>,
   329	) {
   330	    let Some(mut remove_trailing_hunks_from_idx) = remove_trailing_hunks_from_idx else {
   331	        assert!(hunk_token_equal_from.is_none());
   332	        return;
   333	    };
   334	
   335	    let hunk = &mut hunks[remove_trailing_hunks_from_idx];
   336	    let range = range_by_side(hunk);
   337	    if let Some(hunk_token_equal_from) = hunk_token_equal_from {
   338	        let orig_end = range.end;
   339	        let new_end = hunk_token_equal_from;
   340	        range.end = new_end;
   341	        if Range::<u32>::is_empty(range) {
   342	            range.end = orig_end;
   343	        } else if let Some(out) = out_hunks.as_deref_mut() {
   344	            remove_trailing_hunks_from_idx += 1;
   345	            let mut removed_hunk = hunk.clone();
   346	            let new_range = range_by_side(&mut removed_hunk);
   347	
   348	            new_range.start = new_end;
   349	            new_range.end = orig_end;
   350	
   351	            out.push(removed_hunk);
   352	        } else {
   353	            remove_trailing_hunks_from_idx += 1;
   354	        }
   355	    }
   356	    if let Some(out) = out_hunks {
   357	        out.extend_from_slice(&hunks[remove_trailing_hunks_from_idx..]);
   358	    }
   359	    hunks.truncate(remove_trailing_hunks_from_idx);
   360	}
   361	
   362	/// Return an iterator over `(token_idx, hunk_idx, hunk_side)` from `hunks`.
   363	fn iterate_hunks(hunks: &[Hunk]) -> impl Iterator<Item = (u32, usize, Side)> + '_ {
   364	    hunks.iter().enumerate().flat_map(|(hunk_idx, hunk)| {
   365	        match hunk.side {
   366	            Side::Current | Side::Other => &hunk.after,
   367	            Side::Ancestor => &hunk.before,
   368	        }
   369	        .clone()
   370	        .map(move |idx| (idx, hunk_idx, hunk.side))
   371	    })
   372	}
   373	
   374	/// Return a reverse iterator over `(token_idx, hunk_idx, hunk_side)` from `hunks`.
   375	fn iterate_hunks_rev(hunks: &[Hunk]) -> impl Iterator<Item = (u32, usize, Side)> + '_ {
   376	    hunks.iter().enumerate().rev().flat_map(|(hunk_idx, hunk)| {
   377	        match hunk.side {
   378	            Side::Current | Side::Other => &hunk.after,
   379	            Side::Ancestor => &hunk.before,
   380	        }
   381	        .clone()
   382	        .rev()
   383	        .map(move |idx| (idx, hunk_idx, hunk.side))
   384	    })
   385	}
   386	
   387	pub fn write_hunks(
   388	    hunks: &[Hunk],
   389	    input: &imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
   390	    current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
   391	    out: &mut Vec<u8>,
   392	) {
   393	    for hunk in hunks {
   394	        let (tokens, range) = match hunk.side {
   395	            Side::Current => (current_tokens, &hunk.after),
   396	            Side::Other => (input.after.as_slice(), &hunk.after),
   397	            Side::Ancestor => (input.before.as_slice(), &hunk.before),
   398	        };
   399	        write_tokens(&input.interner, &tokens[usize_range(range)], out);
   400	    }
   401	}
   402	
   403	fn usize_range(range: &Range<u32>) -> Range<usize> {
   404	    range.start as usize..range.end as usize
   405	}
   406	
   407	fn write_tokens(interner: &imara_diff::Interner<&[u8]>, tokens: &[imara_diff::Token], out: &mut Vec<u8>) {
   408	    for token in tokens {
   409	        out.extend_from_slice(interner[*token]);
   410	    }
   411	}

   413	/// Find all hunks in `iter` which aren't from the same side as `hunk` and intersect with it.
   414	/// Also put `hunk` into `input` so it's the first item, and possibly put more hunks of the side of `hunk` so
   415	/// `iter` doesn't have any overlapping hunks left.
   416	/// Return `Some` if `intersecting` is non-empty after the operation, indicating overlapping hunks were found.
   417	pub fn take_intersecting(
   418	    iter: &mut Peekable<impl Iterator<Item = Hunk>>,
   419	    input: &mut Vec<Hunk>,
   420	    intersecting: &mut Vec<Hunk>,

   426	    fn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {

   434	        while iter.peek().filter(|b_hunk| left_overlaps_right(b_hunk, hunk)).is_some() {
   435	            intersecting.extend(iter.next());

   476	pub fn collect_hunks(
   477	    algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm,
   478	    input: &imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
   479	    side: Side,
   480	    mut hunks: Vec<Hunk>,
   481	) -> Vec<Hunk> {
   482	    hunks.extend(imara_diff::Diff::compute(algorithm, input).hunks().map(|hunk| Hunk {
   483	        before: hunk.before,

     3	use bstr::BStr;

     5	/// The way the built-in [text driver](crate::blob::BuiltinDriver::Text) will express
     6	/// merge conflicts in the resulting file.
     7	#[derive(Default, Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Ord, PartialOrd, Hash)]
     8	pub enum ConflictStyle {
     9	    /// Only show the zealously minified conflicting lines of the local changes and the incoming (other) changes,
    10	    /// hiding the base version entirely.
    11	    ///
    12	    /// ```text
    13	    /// line1-changed-by-both
    14	    /// <<<<<<< local
    15	    /// line2-to-be-changed-in-incoming
    16	    /// =======
    17	    /// line2-changed
    18	    /// >>>>>>> incoming
    19	    /// ```
    20	    #[default]
    21	    Merge,
    22	    /// Show non-minimized hunks of local changes, the base, and the incoming (other) changes.
    23	    ///
    24	    /// This mode does not hide any information.
    25	    ///
    26	    /// ```text
    27	    /// <<<<<<< local
    28	    /// line1-changed-by-both
    29	    /// line2-to-be-changed-in-incoming
    30	    /// ||||||| 9a8d80c
    31	    /// line1-to-be-changed-by-both
    32	    /// line2-to-be-changed-in-incoming
    33	    /// =======
    34	    /// line1-changed-by-both
    35	    /// line2-changed
    36	    /// >>>>>>> incoming
    37	    /// ```
    38	    Diff3,
    39	    /// Like [`Diff3](Self::Diff3), but will show *minimized* hunks of local change and the incoming (other) changes,
    40	    /// as well as non-minimized hunks of the base.
    41	    ///
    42	    /// ```text
    43	    /// line1-changed-by-both
    44	    /// <<<<<<< local
    45	    /// line2-to-be-changed-in-incoming
    46	    /// ||||||| 9a8d80c
    47	    /// line1-to-be-changed-by-both
    48	    /// line2-to-be-changed-in-incoming
    49	    /// =======
    50	    /// line2-changed
    51	    /// >>>>>>> incoming
    52	    /// ```
    53	    ZealousDiff3,
    54	}
    55	
    56	/// The set of labels to annotate conflict markers with.
    57	///
    58	/// That way it becomes clearer where the content of conflicts are originating from.
    59	#[derive(Default, Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]
    60	pub struct Labels<'a> {
    61	    /// The label for the common *ancestor*.
    62	    pub ancestor: Option<&'a BStr>,
    63	    /// The label for the *current* (or *our*) side.
    64	    pub current: Option<&'a BStr>,
    65	    /// The label for the *other* (or *their*) side.
    66	    pub other: Option<&'a BStr>,
    67	}
    68	
    69	/// Options for the builtin [text driver](crate::blob::BuiltinDriver::Text).
    70	#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]
    71	pub struct Options {
    72	    /// Determine of the diff will be performed.
    73	    /// Defaults to [`imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers`].
    74	    pub diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm,
    75	    /// Decide what to do to automatically resolve conflicts, or to keep them.
    76	    pub conflict: Conflict,
    77	}
    78	
    79	impl Default for Options {
    80	    fn default() -> Self {
    81	        Options {
    82	            conflict: Default::default(),
    83	            diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers,
    84	        }
    85	    }
    86	}
    87	
    88	/// What to do to resolve a conflict.
    89	#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Ord, PartialOrd, Hash)]
    90	pub enum Conflict {
    91	    /// Keep the conflict by marking it in the source file.
    92	    Keep {
    93	        /// How to visualize conflicts in merged files.
    94	        style: ConflictStyle,
    95	        /// The amount of markers to draw, defaults to 7, i.e. `<<<<<<<`
    96	        marker_size: NonZeroU8,
    97	    },
    98	    /// Chose our side to resolve a conflict.
    99	    ResolveWithOurs,
   100	    /// Chose their side to resolve a conflict.
   101	    ResolveWithTheirs,
   102	    /// Place our and their lines one after another, in any order
   103	    ResolveWithUnion,
   104	}
   105	
   106	impl Conflict {
   107	    /// The amount of conflict marker characters to print by default.
   108	    // TODO: use NonZeroU8::new().unwrap() here once the MSRV supports it.
   109	    pub const DEFAULT_MARKER_SIZE: u8 = 7;
   110	
   111	    /// The amount of conflict markers to print if this instance contains them, or `None` otherwise
   112	    pub fn marker_size(&self) -> Option<u8> {
   113	        match self {
   114	            Conflict::Keep { marker_size, .. } => Some(marker_size.get()),
   115	            Conflict::ResolveWithOurs | Conflict::ResolveWithTheirs | Conflict::ResolveWithUnion => None,
   116	        }
   117	    }
   118	}
   119	
   120	impl Default for Conflict {
   121	    fn default() -> Self {
   122	        Conflict::Keep {
   123	            style: Default::default(),
   124	            marker_size: Conflict::DEFAULT_MARKER_SIZE.try_into().unwrap(),
   125	        }
   126	    }
   127	}

   145	    /// This test reproduces what the fuzzer does, allowing it to accept `Arbitrary` input produced by the fuzzer.
   146	    #[test]
   147	    fn clusterfuzz_timeout_regression() {
   148	        #[derive(Debug, Arbitrary)]
   149	        struct FuzzCtx<'a> {
   150	            base: &'a [u8],
   151	            ours: &'a [u8],
   152	            theirs: &'a [u8],
   153	            marker_size: NonZero<u8>,
   154	        }
   155	        fn run_fuzz_case(ours: &[u8], base: &[u8], theirs: &[u8], marker_size: NonZero<u8>) {
   156	            let mut out = Vec::new();
   157	            let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
   158	            for diff_algorithm in [
   159	                imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram,
   160	                imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers,
   161	                imara_diff::Algorithm::MyersMinimal,
   162	            ] {
   163	                let mut options = builtin_driver::text::Options {
   164	                    diff_algorithm,
   165	                    conflict: Default::default(),
   166	                };
   167	                for (left, right) in [(ours, theirs), (theirs, ours)] {
   168	                    let resolution = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text(
   169	                        &mut out,
   170	                        &mut input,
   171	                        Default::default(),
   172	                        left,
   173	                        base,
   174	                        right,
   175	                        options,
   176	                    );
   177	                    if resolution == Resolution::Conflict {
   178	                        for conflict in [
   179	                            Conflict::ResolveWithOurs,
   180	                            Conflict::ResolveWithTheirs,
   181	                            Conflict::ResolveWithUnion,
   182	                            Conflict::Keep {
   183	                                style: ConflictStyle::Diff3,
   184	                                marker_size,
   185	                            },
   186	                            Conflict::Keep {
   187	                                style: ConflictStyle::ZealousDiff3,
   188	                                marker_size,
   189	                            },
   190	                        ] {
   191	                            options.conflict = conflict;
   192	                            gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text(
   193	                                &mut out,
   194	                                &mut input,
   195	                                Default::default(),
   196	                                left,
   197	                                base,
   198	                                right,
   199	                                options,
   200	                            );
   201	                        }
   202	                    }
   203	                }
   204	            }
   205	        }
   206	
   207	        let ctx = FuzzCtx::arbitrary(&mut arbitrary::Unstructured::new(include_bytes!(
   208	            "../../fixtures/clusterfuzz-testcase-minimized-gix-merge-blob-6377298803884032"
   209	        )))
   210	        .expect("testcase matches the historical fuzz target input layout");
   211	
   212	        run_fuzz_case(ctx.ours, ctx.base, ctx.theirs, ctx.marker_size);
   213	    }

   218	        for (baseline, diverging, expected_percentage) in [
   219	            ("baseline.cases", DIVERGING, 10),

   222	            let cases = std::fs::read_to_string(root.join(baseline))?;
   223	            let mut out = Vec::new();

   225	            let mut num_cases = 0;

   227	                num_cases += 1;
   228	                let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();

   230	                    &mut out,
   231	                    &mut input,

   235	                    &case.theirs,
   236	                    case.options,
   237	                );
   238	                if is_case_diverging(&case, diverging) {
   239	                    num_diverging += 1;
   240	                } else {
   241	                    if case.expected.contains_str("<<<<<<<") {
   242	                        assert_eq!(actual, Resolution::Conflict, "{}: resolution mismatch", case.name);
   243	                    } else {
   244	                        assert!(
   245	                            matches!(
   246	                                actual,
   247	                                Resolution::Complete | Resolution::CompleteWithAutoResolvedConflict
   248	                            ),
   249	                            "{}: resolution mismatch",
   250	                            case.name
   251	                        );
   252	                    }
   253	                    assert_str_eq!(
   254	                        out.as_bstr().to_str_lossy(),
   255	                        case.expected.to_str_lossy(),
   256	                        "{}: output mismatch\n{}",
   257	                        case.name,
   258	                        out.as_bstr()
   259	                    );
   260	                    assert_eq!(out.as_bstr(), case.expected);

   372	    mod baseline {
   373	        use std::path::Path;
   374	
   375	        use bstr::BString;
   376	        use gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::{Conflict, ConflictStyle};
   377	
   378	        #[derive(Debug)]
   379	        pub struct Expectation {
   380	            pub ours: BString,
   381	            pub ours_marker: String,
   382	            pub theirs: BString,
   383	            pub theirs_marker: String,
   384	            pub base: BString,
   385	            pub base_marker: String,
   386	            pub name: BString,
   387	            pub expected: BString,
   388	            pub options: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Options,
   389	        }
   390	
   391	        impl Expectation {
   392	            pub fn labels(&self) -> gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Labels<'_> {
   393	                gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Labels {
   394	                    ancestor: Some(self.base_marker.as_str().as_ref()),
   395	                    current: Some(self.ours_marker.as_str().as_ref()),
   396	                    other: Some(self.theirs_marker.as_str().as_ref()),
   397	                }
   398	            }
   399	        }
   400	
   401	        pub struct Expectations<'a> {
   402	            root: &'a Path,
   403	            lines: std::str::Lines<'a>,
   404	        }
   405	
   406	        impl<'a> Expectations<'a> {
   407	            pub fn new(root: &'a Path, cases: &'a str) -> Self {
   408	                Expectations {
   409	                    root,
   410	                    lines: cases.lines(),
   411	                }
   412	            }
   413	        }
   414	
   415	        impl Iterator for Expectations<'_> {
   416	            type Item = Expectation;
   417	
   418	            fn next(&mut self) -> Option<Self::Item> {
   419	                let line = self.lines.next()?;
   420	                let mut words = line.split(' ');
   421	                let (Some(ours), Some(base), Some(theirs), Some(output)) =
   422	                    (words.next(), words.next(), words.next(), words.next())
   423	                else {
   424	                    panic!("need at least the input and output")
   425	                };
   426	
   427	                let read = |rela_path: &str| read_blob(self.root, rela_path);
   428	
   429	                let mut options = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Options::default();
   430	                let marker_size = 7.try_into().unwrap();
   431	                for arg in words {
   432	                    options.conflict = match arg {
   433	                        "--diff3" => Conflict::Keep {
   434	                            style: ConflictStyle::Diff3,
   435	                            marker_size,
   436	                        },
   437	                        "--zdiff3" => Conflict::Keep {
   438	                            style: ConflictStyle::ZealousDiff3,
   439	                            marker_size,
   440	                        },
   441	                        "--ours" => Conflict::ResolveWithOurs,
   442	                        "--theirs" => Conflict::ResolveWithTheirs,
   443	                        "--union" => Conflict::ResolveWithUnion,
   444	                        _ => panic!("Unknown argument to parse into options: '{arg}'"),
   445	                    }
   446	                }
   447	                if output.contains("histogram") {
   448	                    options.diff_algorithm = imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram;
   449	                }
   450	
   451	                Some(Expectation {
   452	                    ours: read(ours),
   453	                    ours_marker: ours.into(),
   454	                    theirs: read(theirs),
   455	                    theirs_marker: theirs.into(),
   456	                    base: read(base),
   457	                    base_marker: base.into(),
   458	                    expected: read(output),
   459	                    name: output.into(),
   460	                    options,
   461	                })
   462	            }
   463	        }
   464	
   465	        fn read_blob(root: &Path, rela_path: &str) -> BString {
   466	            std::fs::read(root.join(rela_path))
   467	                .unwrap_or_else(|err| panic!("Failed to read '{rela_path}' in '{}': {err}", root.display()))
   468	                .into()
   469	        }
   470	    }
   471	}
   472

use gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text;
fn main() {
    let base=b"A\nCOMMENT\nB\n";
    let ours=b"A\nX\nCOMMENT\nB\n";
    let theirs=b"A\nB\n";
    for alg in [imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram] {
      let mut out=Vec::new();
      let mut input=imara_diff::InternedInput::new(&[][..], &[][..]);
      let res=gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text(&mut out,&mut input,Default::default(),ours,base,theirs,text::Options{diff_algorithm:alg, conflict:Default::default()});
      println!("{alg:?} {res:?}\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
    }
}

fn resolve_insertion_deletion_overlap(
    a: &[Hunk],
    b: &[Hunk],
    input: &imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
    current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
) -> Option<Vec<u8>> {
    let (insertion, deletion) = match (change_kind(a), change_kind(b)) {
        (ChangeKind::Insertion, ChangeKind::Deletion) => (a, b),
        (ChangeKind::Deletion, ChangeKind::Insertion) => (b, a),
        _ => return None,
    };

    let mut inserted = Vec::new();
    write_hunks(insertion, input, current_tokens, &mut inserted);
    let mut deleted = Vec::new();
    write_hunks(deletion, input, current_tokens, &mut deleted);

    let mut pos = 0;
    let mut found = false;
    for start in line_starts(&inserted) {
        if inserted[start..].starts_with(&deleted) {
            pos = start;
            found = true;
        }
    }
    found.then(|| {
        let mut out = inserted;
        out.drain(pos..pos + deleted.len());
        out
    })
}

#[derive(PartialEq)]
enum ChangeKind {
    Insertion,
    Deletion,
    Other,
}

fn change_kind(hunks: &[Hunk]) -> ChangeKind {
    let mut has_inserted_lines = false;
    let mut has_deleted_lines = false;
    for hunk in hunks {
        match hunk.side {
            Side::Current | Side::Other => {
                if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
                    has_inserted_lines = true;
                }
            }
            Side::Ancestor => has_deleted_lines = true,
        }
    }
    match (has_inserted_lines, has_deleted_lines) {
        (true, false) => ChangeKind::Insertion,
        (false, true) => ChangeKind::Deletion,
        _ => ChangeKind::Other,
    }
}

fn line_starts(buf: &[u8]) -> impl Iterator<Item = usize> + '"'"'_ {
    std::iter::once(0).chain(
        buf.iter()
            .enumerate()
            .filter_map(|(idx, byte)| (*byte == b'"'"'\n'"'"').then_some(idx + 1))
            .filter(|idx| *idx < buf.len()),
    )
}

   228	fn first_hunk<'a>(front: &'a [Hunk], ours: &'a [Hunk], theirs: &'a [Hunk], back: &'a [Hunk]) -> &'a Hunk {
   229	    front
   230	        .first()
   231	        .or(ours.first())
   232	        .or(theirs.first())
   233	        .or(back.first())
   234	        .expect("at least one hunk - we aborted if there are none anywhere")
   235	}

   237	/// Note that last-hunk could be [`first_hunk()`], so the hunk must only be used accordingly.
   238	fn last_hunk<'a>(front: &'a [Hunk], ours: &'a [Hunk], theirs: &'a [Hunk], back: &'a [Hunk]) -> &'a Hunk {
   239	    back.last()
   240	        .or(theirs.last())
   241	        .or(ours.last())
   242	        .or(front.last())
   243	        .expect("at least one hunk - we aborted if there are none anywhere")
   244	}

   246	fn before_range_from_hunks(hunks: &[Hunk]) -> Range<u32> {
   247	
   248	fn resolve_insertion_deletion_overlap(
   249	    a: &[Hunk],
   250	    b: &[Hunk],
   251	    input: &imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
   252	    current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
   253	) -> Option<Vec<u8>> {
   254	    let (insertion, deletion) = match (change_kind(a), change_kind(b)) {
   255	        (ChangeKind::Insertion, ChangeKind::Deletion) => (a, b),
   256	        (ChangeKind::Deletion, ChangeKind::Insertion) => (b, a),
   257	        _ => return None,
   258	    };
   259	
   260	    let mut inserted = Vec::new();
   261	    write_hunks(insertion, input, current_tokens, &mut inserted);
   262	    let mut deleted = Vec::new();
   263	    write_hunks(deletion, input, current_tokens, &mut deleted);
   264	
   265	    let mut pos = 0;
   266	    let mut found = false;
   267	    for start in line_starts(&inserted) {
   268	        if inserted[start..].starts_with(&deleted) {
   269	            pos = start;
   270	            found = true;
   271	        }
   272	    }
   273	    found.then(|| {
   274	        let mut out = inserted;
   275	        out.drain(pos..pos + deleted.len());
   276	        out
   277	    })
   278	}
   279	
   280	#[derive(PartialEq)]
   281	enum ChangeKind {
   282	    Insertion,
   283	    Deletion,
   284	    Other,
   285	}
   286	
   287	fn change_kind(hunks: &[Hunk]) -> ChangeKind {
   288	    let mut has_inserted_lines = false;
   289	    let mut has_deleted_lines = false;
   290	    for hunk in hunks {
   291	        match hunk.side {
   292	            Side::Current | Side::Other => {
   293	                if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
   294	                    has_inserted_lines = true;
   295	                }
   296	            }
   297	            Side::Ancestor => has_deleted_lines = true,
   298	        }
   299	    }
   300	    match (has_inserted_lines, has_deleted_lines) {
   301	        (true, false) => ChangeKind::Insertion,
   302	        (false, true) => ChangeKind::Deletion,
   303	        _ => ChangeKind::Other,
   304	    }
   305	}
   306	
   307	fn line_starts(buf: &[u8]) -> impl Iterator<Item = usize> + '_ {
   308	    std::iter::once(0).chain(
   309	        buf.iter()
   310	            .enumerate()
   311	            .filter_map(|(idx, byte)| (*byte == b'\n').then_some(idx + 1))
   312	            .filter(|idx| *idx < buf.len()),
   313	    )
   314	}
   315	
   316	    hunks
   317	        .first()
   318	        .zip(hunks.last())
   319	        .map(|(f, l)| f.before.start..l.before.end)
   320	        .expect("at least one entry")
   321	}
   322

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/gix-merge/src/blob/builtin_driver/text/function.rs   --old_str 'fn resolve_insertion_deletion_overlap(
    a: &[Hunk],
    b: &[Hunk],
    input: &imara_diff::InternedInput<&[u8]>,
    current_tokens: &[imara_diff::Token],
) -> Option<Vec<u8>> {
    let (insertion, deletion) = match (change_kind(a), change_kind(b)) {
        (ChangeKind::Insertion, ChangeKind::Deletion) => (a, b),
        (ChangeKind::Deletion, ChangeKind::Insertion) => (b, a),
        _ => return None,
    };

    let mut inserted = Vec::new();
    write_hunks(insertion, input, current_tokens, &mut inserted);
    let mut deleted = Vec::new();
    write_hunks(deletion, input, current_tokens, &mut deleted);

    let mut pos = 0;
    let mut found = false;
    for start in line_starts(&inserted) {
        if inserted[start..].starts_with(&deleted) {
            pos = start;
            found = true;
        }
    }
    found.then(|| {
        let mut out = inserted;
        out.drain(pos..pos + deleted.len());
        out
    })
}

#[derive(PartialEq)]
enum ChangeKind {
    Insertion,
    Deletion,
    Other,
}

fn change_kind(hunks: &[Hunk]) -> ChangeKind {
    let mut has_inserted_lines = false;
    let mut has_deleted_lines = false;
    for hunk in hunks {
        match hunk.side {
            Side::Current | Side::Other => {
                if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
                    has_inserted_lines = true;
                }
            }
            Side::Ancestor => has_deleted_lines = true,
        }
    }
    match (has_inserted_lines, has_deleted_lines) {
        (true, false) => ChangeKind::Insertion,
        (false, true) => ChangeKind::Deletion,
        _ => ChangeKind::Other,
    }
}

fn line_starts(buf: &[u8]) -> impl Iterator<Item = usize> + '"'"'_ {
    std::iter::once(0).chain(
        buf.iter()
            .enumerate()
            .filter_map(|(idx, byte)| (*byte == b'"'"'\n'"'"').then_some(idx + 1))
            .filter(|idx| *idx < buf.len()),
    )
}

     1	// Modified for gitoxide from the upstream imara-diff crate.
     2	// Upstream source: git cat-file -p 32d1e45d3df061e6ccba6db7fdce92db29e345d8:src/lib.rs
     3	
     4	#![deny(missing_docs)]
     5	//! Imara-diff is a solid (imara in Swahili) diff library for Rust.
     6	//! Solid refers to the fact that imara-diff provides very good runtime performance even
     7	//! in pathological cases so that your application never appears to freeze while waiting on a diff.
     8	//! The performance improvements are achieved using battle tested heuristics used in gnu-diff and git
     9	//! that are known to yield fast runtime and performance.
    10	//!
    11	//! Imara-diff is also designed to be flexible so that it can be used with arbitrary collections and
    12	//! not just lists and strings and even allows reusing large parts of the computation when
    13	//! comparing the same file to multiple different files.
    14	//!
    15	//! Imara-diff provides two diff algorithms:
    16	//!
    17	//! * The linear-space variant of the well known [**Myers** algorithm](http://www.xmailserver.org/diff2.pdf)
    18	//! * The **Histogram** algorithm which is a variant of the patience diff algorithm.
    19	//!
    20	//! Myers algorithm has been enhanced with preprocessing and multiple heuristics to ensure fast runtime in pathological
    21	//! cases to avoid quadratic time complexity and closely matches the behavior of gnu-diff and git.
    22	//! The Histogram algorithm was originally ported from git but has been heavily optimized.
    23	//! The **Histogram algorithm outperforms Myers diff** by 10% - 100% across a **wide variety of workloads**.
    24	//!
    25	//! Imara-diffs algorithms have been benchmarked over a wide variety of real-world code.
    26	//! For example, while comparing multiple different Linux kernel versions, it performs up to 30 times better than the `similar` crate.
    27	//!
    28	//! # API Overview
    29	//!
    30	//! ## Preparing the input
    31	//! To compute a diff, an input sequence is required. `imara-diff` computes diffs on abstract
    32	//! sequences represented as a slice of IDs/tokens: [`Token`]. To create
    33	//! such a sequence from your input type (for example, text), the input needs to be interned.
    34	//! For that `imara-diff` provides utilities in the form of the [`InternedInput`] struct and
    35	//! the `TokenSource` trait to construct it. [`InternedInput`] contains the two sides of
    36	//! the diff (used while computing the diff). As well as the interner that allows mapping
    37	//! back tokens to their original data.
    38	//!
    39	//! The most common use case for diff is comparing text. `&str` implements `TokenSource`
    40	//! by default to segment the text into lines. So creating an input for a text-based diff usually
    41	//! looks something like the following:
    42	//!
    43	//! ```
    44	//! # use gix_imara_diff::InternedInput;
    45	//! #
    46	//! let before = "abc\ndef";
    47	//! let after = "abc\ndefg";
    48	//! let input = InternedInput::new(before, after);
    49	//! assert_eq!(input.interner[input.before[0]], "abc\n");
    50	//! ```
    51	//!
    52	//! Note that interning inputs is optional, and you could choose a different strategy
    53	//! for creating a sequence of tokens. Instead of using the [`Diff::compute`] function,
    54	//! [`Diff::compute_with`] can be used to provide a list of tokens directly, entirely
    55	//! bypassing the interning step.
    56	//!
    57	//! ## Computing the Diff
    58	//!
    59	//! A diff of two sequences is represented by the [`Diff`] struct and computed by
    60	//! [`Diff::compute`] / [`Diff::compute_with`]. An algorithm can also be chosen here.
    61	//! In most situations, [`Algorithm::Histogram`] is a good choice; refer to the docs
    62	//! of [`Algorithm`] for more details.
    63	//!
    64	//! After the initial computation, the diff can be *postprocessed*. If the diff is shown
    65	//! to a human in some way (even indirectly), you always want to use this.
    66	//!
    67	//! However, when only counting the number of changed tokens quickly, this can be skipped.
    68	//! The postprocessing allows you to provide your own
    69	//! heuristic for selecting a slider position. An indentation-based heuristic is provided,
    70	//! which is a good fit for all text-based line diffs. The internals of the heuristic are
    71	//! public, so a tweaked heuristic can be built on top.
    72	//!
    73	//! ```
    74	//! # use gix_imara_diff::{InternedInput, Diff, Algorithm};
    75	//! #
    76	//! let before = "abc\ndef";
    77	//! let after = "abc\ndefg";
    78	//! let input = InternedInput::new(before, after);
    79	//! let mut diff = Diff::compute(Algorithm::Histogram, &input);
    80	//! diff.postprocess_lines(&input);
    81	//! assert!(!diff.is_removed(0) && !diff.is_added(0));
    82	//! assert!(diff.is_removed(1) && diff.is_added(1));
    83	//! ```
    84	//!
    85	//! ## Accessing results
    86	//!
    87	//! [`Diff`] allows querying whether a particular position was removed/added on either
    88	//! side of the diff with [`Diff::is_removed`] / [`Diff::is_added`]. The number
    89	//! of additions/removals can be quickly counted with [`Diff::count_removals`] /
    90	//! [`Diff::count_additions`]. The most powerful/useful interface is the hunk iterator
    91	//! [`Diff::hunks`], which returns a list of additions/removals/modifications in the
    92	//! order that they appear in the input.
    93	//!
    94	//! Finally, when built with the `unified_diff` feature, this crate also provides a
    95	//! built-in unified diff/patch formatter similar to `git diff` or `diff -u`.
    96	//! Note that while the formatter has a decent amount of flexibility, it is fairly
    97	//! simplistic and not every formatting may be possible. It's meant to cover common
    98	//! situations but not cover every advanced use case. Instead, if you need more advanced
    99	//! printing, build your own printer on top of the [`Diff::hunks`] iterator; for that, you can
   100	//! take inspiration from the built-in printer implementation.
   101	//!
   102	//! ```
   103	//! # use gix_imara_diff::{InternedInput, Diff, Algorithm, BasicLineDiffPrinter, UnifiedDiffConfig};
   104	//! #
   105	//!
   106	//! let before = r#"fn foo() -> Bar {
   107	//!     let mut foo = 2;
   108	//!     foo *= 50;
   109	//!     println!("hello world")
   110	//! }
   111	//! "#;
   112	//!
   113	//! let after = r#"// lorem ipsum
   114	//! fn foo() -> Bar {
   115	//!     let mut foo = 2;
   116	//!     foo *= 50;
   117	//!     println!("hello world");
   118	//!     println!("{foo}");
   119	//! }
   120	//! // foo
   121	//! "#;
   122	//! let input = InternedInput::new(before, after);
   123	//! let mut diff = Diff::compute(Algorithm::Histogram, &input);
   124	//! diff.postprocess_lines(&input);
   125	//!
   126	//! assert_eq!(
   127	//!     diff.unified_diff(
   128	//!         &BasicLineDiffPrinter(&input.interner),
   129	//!         UnifiedDiffConfig::default(),
   130	//!         &input,
   131	//!     )
   132	//!     .to_string(),
   133	//!     r#"@@ -1,5 +1,8 @@
   134	//! +// lorem ipsum
   135	//!  fn foo() -> Bar {
   136	//!      let mut foo = 2;
   137	//!      foo *= 50;
   138	//! -    println!("hello world")
   139	//! +    println!("hello world");
   140	//! +    println!("{foo}");

   176	pub enum Algorithm {
   177	    /// A variation of the [`patience` diff algorithm described by Bram Cohen's blog post](https://bramcohen.livejournal.com/73318.html)
   178	    /// that uses a histogram to find the least common LCS.
   179	    /// Just like the `patience` diff algorithm, this algorithm usually produces
   180	    /// more human-readable output than Myers algorithm.
   181	    /// However, compared to the `patience` diff algorithm (which is slower than Myers algorithm),
   182	    /// the Histogram algorithm performs much better.
   183	    ///
   184	    /// The implementation here was originally ported from `git` but has been significantly
   185	    /// modified to improve performance.
   186	    /// As a result, it consistently **performs better than Myers algorithm** (5%-100%) over
   187	    /// a wide variety of test data.
   188	    ///
   189	    /// For pathological subsequences that only contain highly repeating tokens (64+ occurrences)
   190	    /// the algorithm falls back on Myers algorithm (with heuristics) to avoid quadratic behavior.
   191	    ///
   192	    /// Compared to Myers algorithm, the Histogram diff algorithm is more focused on providing
   193	    /// human-readable diffs instead of minimal diffs. In practice, this means that the edit sequences
   194	    /// produced by the histogram diff are often longer than those produced by Myers algorithm.
   195	    ///
   196	    /// The heuristic used by the histogram diff does not work well for inputs with small (often repeated)
   197	    /// tokens. For example, **character diffs do not work well** as most (English) text is made up of
   198	    /// a fairly small set of characters. The `Histogram` algorithm will automatically detect these cases and
   199	    /// fall back to Myers algorithm. However, this detection has a nontrivial overhead, so
   200	    /// if it's known upfront that the sort of tokens is very small, `Myers` algorithm should
   201	    /// be used instead.
   202	    #[default]
   203	    Histogram,
   204	    /// An implementation of the linear space variant of
   205	    /// [Myers  `O((N+M)D)` algorithm](http://www.xmailserver.org/diff2.pdf).
   206	    /// The algorithm is enhanced with preprocessing that removes
   207	    /// tokens that don't occur in the other file at all.
   208	    /// Furthermore, two heuristics for the middle snake search are implemented
   209	    /// that ensure reasonable runtime (mostly linear time complexity) even for large files.
   210	    ///
   211	    /// Due to the divide-and-conquer nature of the algorithm,
   212	    /// the edit sequences produced are still fairly small even when the middle snake
   213	    /// search is aborted by a heuristic.
   214	    /// However, the produced edit sequences are not guaranteed to be fully minimal.
   215	    /// If that property is vital to you, use the `MyersMinimal` algorithm instead.
   216	    ///
   217	    /// The implementation (including the preprocessing) is mostly
   218	    /// ported from `git` and `gnu-diff`, where Myers algorithm is used
   219	    /// as the default diff algorithm.
   220	    /// Therefore, the used heuristics have been heavily battle-tested and
   221	    /// are known to behave well over a large variety of inputs.
   222	    Myers,
   223	    /// Same as `Myers` but the early abort heuristics are disabled to guarantee
   224	    /// a minimal edit sequence.
   225	    /// This can mean significant slowdown in pathological cases.
   226	    MyersMinimal,
   227	}
   228	
   229	/// Represents the difference between two sequences of tokens.
   230	///
   231	/// A `Diff` stores which tokens were removed from the first sequence and which tokens were added to the second sequence.
   232	#[derive(Default)]
   233	pub struct Diff {
   234	    /// Tracks which tokens were removed from the first sequence (`before`), with
   235	    /// one entry for each one in the `before` sequence.
   236	    removed: Vec<bool>,
   237	    /// Tracks which tokens were added to the second sequence (`after`), with
   238	    /// one entry for each one in the `after` sequence.
   239	    added: Vec<bool>,
   240	}
   241	
   242	impl std::fmt::Debug for Diff {
   243	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {
   244	        f.debug_list().entries(self.hunks()).finish()
   245	    }
   246	}
   247	
   248	impl Diff {
   249	    /// Computes an edit-script that transforms `input.before` into `input.after` using
   250	    /// the specified `algorithm`
   251	    pub fn compute<T>(algorithm: Algorithm, input: &InternedInput<T>) -> Diff {
   252	        let mut diff = Diff::default();
   253	        diff.compute_with(algorithm, &input.before, &input.after, input.interner.num_tokens());
   254	        diff
   255	    }
   256	
   257	    /// Computes an edit-script that transforms `before` into `after` using
   258	    /// the specified `algorithm`.
   259	    pub fn compute_with(&mut self, algorithm: Algorithm, mut before: &[Token], mut after: &[Token], num_tokens: u32) {
   260	        assert!(
   261	            before.len() < i32::MAX as usize,
   262	            "imara-diff only supports up to {} tokens",
   263	            i32::MAX
   264	        );
   265	        assert!(
   266	            after.len() < i32::MAX as usize,
   267	            "imara-diff only supports up to {} tokens",
   268	            i32::MAX
   269	        );
   270	        self.removed.clear();
   271	        self.added.clear();
   272	        self.removed.resize(before.len(), false);
   273	        self.added.resize(after.len(), false);
   274	        let common_prefix = strip_common_prefix(&mut before, &mut after) as usize;
   275	        let common_postfix = strip_common_postfix(&mut before, &mut after);
   276	        let range = common_prefix..self.removed.len() - common_postfix as usize;
   277	        let removed = &mut self.removed[range];
   278	        let range = common_prefix..self.added.len() - common_postfix as usize;
   279	        let added = &mut self.added[range];
   280	        match algorithm {
   281	            Algorithm::Histogram => histogram::diff(before, after, removed, added, num_tokens),
   282	            Algorithm::Myers => myers::diff(before, after, removed, added, false),
   283	            Algorithm::MyersMinimal => myers::diff(before, after, removed, added, true),
   284	        }
   285	    }
   286	
   287	    /// Returns the total number of tokens that were added in the second sequence.
   288	    pub fn count_additions(&self) -> u32 {
   289	        self.added.iter().map(|&added| u32::from(added)).sum()
   290	    }
   291	
   292	    /// Returns the total number of tokens that were removed from the first sequence (`before`).
   293	    pub fn count_removals(&self) -> u32 {
   294	        self.removed.iter().map(|&removed| u32::from(removed)).sum()
   295	    }
   296	
   297	    /// Returns `true` if the token at the given index was removed from the first sequence (`before`).
   298	    ///
   299	    /// # Panics
   300	    ///
   301	    /// Panics if `token_idx` is out of bounds for the first sequence.
   302	    pub fn is_removed(&self, token_idx: u32) -> bool {
   303	        self.removed[token_idx as usize]
   304	    }
   305	
   306	    /// Returns `true` if the token at the given index was added to the second sequence (`after`).
   307	    ///
   308	    /// # Panics
   309	    ///
   310	    /// Panics if `token_idx` is out of bounds for the second sequence (`after`).
   311	    pub fn is_added(&self, token_idx: u32) -> bool {
   312	        self.added[token_idx as usize]
   313	    }
   314	
   315	    /// Postprocesses the diff to make it more human-readable. Certain hunks
   316	    /// have an ambiguous placement (even in a minimal diff) where they can move
   317	    /// downward or upward by removing a token (line) at the start and adding
   318	    /// one at the end (or the other way around). The postprocessing adjusts
   319	    /// these hunks according to a couple of rules:
   320	    ///
   321	    /// * Always merge multiple hunks if possible.
   322	    /// * Always try to create a single MODIFY hunk instead of multiple disjoint
   323	    ///   ADDED/REMOVED hunks.
   324	    /// * Move sliders as far down as possible.
   325	    pub fn postprocess_no_heuristic<T>(&mut self, input: &InternedInput<T>) {
   326	        self.postprocess_with_heuristic(input, NoSliderHeuristic)
   327	    }
   328	
   329	    /// Postprocesses the diff to make it more human-readable. Certain hunks
   330	    /// have an ambiguous placement (even in a minimal diff) where they can move
   331	    /// downward or upward by removing a token (line) at the start and adding
   332	    /// one at the end (or the other way around). The postprocessing adjusts
   333	    /// these hunks according to a couple of rules:
   334	    ///
   335	    /// * Always merge multiple hunks if possible.
   336	    /// * Always try to create a single MODIFY hunk instead of multiple disjoint
   337	    ///   ADDED/REMOVED hunks.
   338	    /// * Based on a line's indentation level, heuristically compute the most
   339	    ///   intuitive location to split lines.
   340	    /// * Move sliders as far down as possible.
   341	    pub fn postprocess_lines<T: AsRef<[u8]>>(&mut self, input: &InternedInput<T>) {
   342	        self.postprocess_with_heuristic(
   343	            input,
   344	            IndentHeuristic::new(|token| {
   345	                IndentLevel::for_ascii_line(input.interner[token].as_ref().iter().copied(), 8)
   346	            }),
   347	        )
   348	    }
   349	
   350	    /// Return an iterator that yields the changed hunks in this diff.
   351	    pub fn hunks(&self) -> HunkIter<'_> {
   352	        HunkIter {
   353	            removed: self.removed.iter(),
   354	            added: self.added.iter(),
   355	            pos_before: 0,
   356	            pos_after: 0,
   357	        }
   358	    }
   359	}
   360	
   361	/// A single change in a `Diff` that represents a range of tokens (`before`)
   362	/// in the first sequence that were replaced by a different range of tokens
   363	/// in the second sequence (`after`).
   364	///
   365	/// Each hunk identifies a contiguous region of change, where tokens from the `before` range
   366	/// should be replaced with tokens from the `after` range.
   367	#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Default)]
   368	pub struct Hunk {
   369	    /// The range of token indices in the first sequence (`before`) that were removed.
   370	    pub before: Range<u32>,
   371	    /// The range of token indices in the second sequence (`after`) that were added.
   372	    pub after: Range<u32>,
   373	}
   374	
   375	impl Hunk {
   376	    /// Can be used instead of `Option::None` for better performance.
   377	    /// Because `imara-diff` does not support more than `i32::MAX` there is an unused bit pattern that can be used.
   378	    ///
   379	    /// It has some nice properties where it usually is not necessary to check for `None` separately:
   380	    /// Empty ranges fail contains checks and also fail smaller than checks.

use gix_merge::blob::{builtin_driver::text, Resolution};
fn merge(alg: imara_diff::Algorithm, ours:&[u8], base:&[u8], theirs:&[u8]) -> (Resolution, Vec<u8>) {
 let mut out=Vec::new(); let mut input=imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
 let res=gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text(&mut out,&mut input,Default::default(),ours,base,theirs,text::Options{diff_algorithm:alg, conflict:Default::default()});
 (res,out)
}
fn bytes(lines:&[String])->Vec<u8>{lines.join("\n").into_bytes().into_iter().chain(std::iter::once(b'\n')).collect()}
fn main(){
 let atoms=["a","b","c","d","e","f","g","h","i","j","x","y","z","// comment","let modal","query"];
 for n in 5..12{
  let total=1usize<<n.min(10);
  for mask in 0..total{
   let mut base=Vec::new();
   for i in 0..n { base.push(atoms[((i*3 + ((mask>> (i%10))&1))%atoms.len())].to_string()); }
   for del in 1..n-1{
    let mut theirs=base.clone(); theirs.remove(del);
    for ins in 1..del+1{
     let mut ours=base.clone();
     let block=(0..8).map(|k| format!("new{}",k)).collect::<Vec<_>>();
     for (off,l) in block.iter().enumerate(){ ours.insert(ins+off,l.clone()); }
     let b=bytes(&base); let o=bytes(&ours); let t=bytes(&theirs);
     let (rm,om)=merge(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers,&o,&b,&t);
     let (rh,oh)=merge(imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram,&o,&b,&t);
     if rm==Resolution::Conflict && rh!=Resolution::Conflict {
       println!("FOUND n={n} mask={mask} ins={ins} del={del}\nbase={:?}\nours={:?}\ntheirs={:?}\nMYERS:\n{}\nHIST:\n{}",base,ours,theirs,String::from_utf8_lossy(&om),String::from_utf8_lossy(&oh));
       return;
     }
    }
   }
  }
 }
 println!("none");
}
EOF

use gix_merge::blob::{builtin_driver::text, Resolution};
fn merge(alg: imara_diff::Algorithm, ours:&[u8], base:&[u8], theirs:&[u8]) -> (Resolution, Vec<u8>) {
 let mut out=Vec::new(); let mut input=imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
 let res=gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text(&mut out,&mut input,Default::default(),ours,base,theirs,text::Options{diff_algorithm:alg, conflict:Default::default()});
 (res,out)
}

  let n=70;
  let mut base=Vec::new();
  for _ in 0..n { base.push(atoms[lcg(&mut seed)%atoms.len()].to_string()); }
  let del=5+lcg(&mut seed)%(n-10);
  base[del]="// ── MCP config modal ─────────────────────────────────────────────".into();
  if del+1<n { base[del+1]="let mcpConfigModal = $state<CodegenMcpConfigModal>();".into(); }
  if del+2<n { base[del+2]="const mcpClaudeConfigQuery = createQuery();".into(); }
  let ins=1+lcg(&mut seed)%del;
  let mut ours=base.clone();
  let ins_len=50+lcg(&mut seed)%50;
  for k in 0..ins_len { ours.insert(ins+k, format!("\t// new code {case}-{k}")); }
  let mut theirs=base.clone(); theirs.remove(del);
  let b=bytes(&base); let o=bytes(&ours); let t=bytes(&theirs);
  let (rm,om)=merge(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers,&o,&b,&t);
  let (rh,oh)=merge(imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram,&o,&b,&t);
  if rm==Resolution::Conflict && rh!=Resolution::Conflict {
    println!("FOUND case={case} ins={ins} del={del} ins_len={ins_len}\nMYERS conflicts={}\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&om).matches("<<<<<<<").count(), String::from_utf8_lossy(&om));

    return;
  }
 }

@@ -215,6 +215,37 @@ pub fn merge<'a>(
     }
     write_ancestor(input, ancestor_integrated_until, input.before.len(), out);
 
+    // Git's Myers diff can choose different hunk boundaries than `imara_diff` for ambiguous edits.
+    // In merge-style conflicts, try Histogram as a fallback to avoid reporting conflicts that can be
+    // resolved cleanly with better hunk alignment.
+    if resolution == Resolution::Conflict
+        && diff_algorithm == imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers
+        && matches!(conflict, Conflict::Keep { style: ConflictStyle::Merge, .. })
+    {
+        let mut histogram_out = Vec::new();
+        let mut histogram_input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(&[][..], &[][..]);
+        let histogram_resolution = merge(
+            &mut histogram_out,
+            &mut histogram_input,
+            Labels {
+                ancestor: ancestor_label,
+                current: current_label,
+                other: other_label,
+            },
+            current,
+            ancestor,
+            other,
+            Options {
+                diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram,
+                conflict,
+            },
+        );
+        if histogram_resolution != Resolution::Conflict {
+            *out = histogram_out;
+            return histogram_resolution;
+        }
+    }
+
     resolution
 }

@@ -215,6 +215,37 @@ pub fn merge<'a>(
     }
     write_ancestor(input, ancestor_integrated_until, input.before.len(), out);
 
+    // Git's Myers diff can choose different hunk boundaries than `imara_diff` for ambiguous edits.
+    // In merge-style conflicts, try Histogram as a fallback to avoid reporting conflicts that can be
+    // resolved cleanly with better hunk alignment.
+    if resolution == Resolution::Conflict
+        && diff_algorithm == imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers
+        && matches!(conflict, Conflict::Keep { style: ConflictStyle::Merge, .. })
+    {
+        let mut histogram_out = Vec::new();
+        let mut histogram_input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(&[][..], &[][..]);
+        let histogram_resolution = merge(
+            &mut histogram_out,
+            &mut histogram_input,
+            Labels {
+                ancestor: ancestor_label,
+                current: current_label,
+                other: other_label,
+            },
+            current,
+            ancestor,
+            other,
+            Options {
+                diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram,
+                conflict,
+            },
+        );
+        if histogram_resolution != Resolution::Conflict {
+            *out = histogram_out;
+            return histogram_resolution;
+        }
+    }
+
     resolution
 }
